<P align="left">
<B><FONT size="2">1)&nbsp;Basis of Presentation and Stock-Based
Compensation</FONT></B>

<DIV>&nbsp;</DIV>

    <TD width="3%"></TD>
    <TD width="97%"></TD>

<TR valign="top">
    <TD></TD>
    <TD>
    <B><I><FONT size="2">Basis of Presentation</FONT></I></B></TD>
</TR>

</TABLE>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">In the opinion of management, the unaudited
interim consolidated condensed financial statements of Applied
Materials, Inc. (Applied) included herein have been prepared on
a basis consistent with the October&nbsp;27, 2002 audited
consolidated financial statements and include all material
adjustments, consisting of normal recurring adjustments,
necessary to fairly present the information set forth therein.
These unaudited interim consolidated condensed financial
statements should be read in conjunction with the audited
consolidated financial statements and notes thereto included in
Applied&#146;s Form&nbsp;10-K for the fiscal year ended
October&nbsp;27, 2002. Applied&#146;s results of operations for
the three and six months ended April&nbsp;27, 2003 are not
necessarily indicative of future operating results.
</FONT>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">The preparation of financial statements in
conformity with generally accepted accounting principles in the
United States of America requires management to make estimates
and assumptions that affect the amounts reported in the
financial statements and accompanying notes. Actual results
could differ materially from those estimates.
</FONT>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">Certain prior year amounts have been reclassified
to conform to the fiscal 2003 financial statement presentation.
</FONT>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">During the second fiscal quarter of 2003, Applied
reviewed the functional currencies of certain subsidiaries in
Europe and Japan and determined that the United States dollar
was more appropriate as the functional currency due to changes
in facts, circumstances, scope of operations and business
practices. The change in functional currencies did not have a
material effect on Applied&#146;s results of operations and
financial position during the second fiscal quarter of 2003.
</FONT>

<DIV>&nbsp;</DIV>

<TABLE width="100%" border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0">

<TR>
    <TD width="3%"></TD>
    <TD width="97%"></TD>
</TR>

<TR valign="top">
    <TD></TD>
    <TD>
    <B><I><FONT size="2">Stock-Based Compensation</FONT></I></B></TD>
</TR>

</TABLE>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">During the second fiscal quarter of 2003,
Statement of Financial Accounting Standards No.&nbsp;148
(SFAS&nbsp;148), &#147;Accounting for Stock-Based
Compensation&nbsp;&#151; Transition and Disclosure&nbsp;&#151;
An Amendment of FASB Statement No.&nbsp;123&#148; became
effective for Applied.
</FONT>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">Applied measures compensation expense for its
stock-based employee compensation plans using the intrinsic
value method. As the exercise price of all options granted under
these plans was equal to the fair market price of the underlying
common stock on the grant date, no stock-based employee
compensation cost is recognized in the consolidated condensed
statements of operations.
</FONT>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">In accordance with SFAS&nbsp;148 and Statement of
Financial Accounting Standards No.&nbsp;123, &#147;Accounting
for Stock-Based Compensation&#148; (SFAS&nbsp;123),
Applied&#146;s option expense is computed using the
Black-Scholes option pricing model. This model was developed for
use in estimating the value of traded options that have no
vesting restrictions and are fully transferable. Applied&#146;s
employee stock options have characteristics significantly
different from those of traded options; therefore, in the
opinion of management, the Black-Scholes option pricing model
required by SFAS&nbsp;148 and SFAS&nbsp;123, does not
necessarily provide a reliable measure of the fair value of
Applied&#146;s options.
</FONT>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">To comply with SFAS 148, Applied is presenting
the following table to illustrate the effect on the net income/
(loss) and earnings/ (loss) per share if it had applied the fair
value recognition provisions of SFAS&nbsp;123, as amended, to
options granted under the stock-based employee compensation
plans. For purposes
</FONT>

<P align="center"><FONT size="2">4
</FONT>

<P align="left">
<B><FONT size="2">2)&nbsp;Earnings/ Loss Per Share</FONT></B>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">Basic earnings/loss per share has been determined
using the weighted average number of common shares outstanding
during the period. Diluted earnings per share has been
determined using the weighted average number of common shares
and equivalents (representing the dilutive effect of stock
options) outstanding during the period. Applied&#146;s net
income/loss has not been adjusted for any period presented for
purposes of computing basic or diluted earnings/loss per share.
</FONT>

<P align="center"><FONT size="2">5
</FONT>

<P><HR noshade><P>
<H5 align="left" style="page-break-before:always">&nbsp;</H5><P>

<DIV align="center">
<B><FONT size="2">APPLIED MATERIALS, INC.</FONT></B>
</DIV>

<P align="center">
<B><FONT size="2">NOTES TO CONSOLIDATED CONDENSED FINANCIAL
STATEMENTS&nbsp;&#151;&nbsp;(Continued)</FONT></B>

<DIV align="center">
<FONT size="2">(Unaudited)
</FONT>
</DIV>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">For purposes of computing diluted earnings/loss
per share, weighted average common share equivalents do not
include stock options with an exercise price that exceeded the
average fair market value of Applied&#146;s common stock for the
period. For the three and six months ended April&nbsp;28, 2002,
options to purchase approximately 15,012,000 and 21,715,000
shares of common stock at an average exercise price of $34.89
and $31.45 were excluded from the computation. For the three and
six months ended April&nbsp;27, 2003, options to purchase
approximately 173,908,000 and 172,698,000 shares of common stock
at an average exercise price of $20.11 and $20.15 were excluded
from the computation.
</FONT>

<P align="left">
<B><FONT size="2">3)&nbsp;Accounts Receivable, Net</FONT></B>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">Applied has agreements with various financial
institutions to sell accounts receivable from selected
customers. Applied sold accounts receivable under these
agreements of $103&nbsp;million and $172&nbsp;million for the
three months ended April&nbsp;28, 2002 and April&nbsp;27, 2003,
respectively, and sold $302&nbsp;million and $294&nbsp;million
for the six months ended April&nbsp;28, 2002 and April&nbsp;27,
2003, respectively. Discounting fees were approximately
$1&nbsp;million and $1.5&nbsp;million for the three months ended
April&nbsp;28, 2002 and April&nbsp;27, 2003, respectively, and
were approximately $2&nbsp;million for each of the six months
ended April&nbsp;28, 2002 and April&nbsp;27, 2003. Discounting
fees were recorded as interest expense. At April&nbsp;27, 2003,
$94&nbsp;million of sold receivables remained outstanding under
these agreements. A portion of these sold receivables is subject
to certain recourse provisions. Applied has not experienced any
losses under these recourse provisions.
</FONT>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">Aggregate amortization expense was
$26&nbsp;million and $24&nbsp;million for the six month periods
ended April&nbsp;28, 2002 and April&nbsp;27, 2003, respectively.
As of April&nbsp;27, 2003, future estimated amortization expense
is expected to be: $24&nbsp;million for the remainder of fiscal
2003, $48&nbsp;million for fiscal 2004, $19&nbsp;million for
fiscal 2005, $13&nbsp;million for fiscal 2006, $5&nbsp;million
for fiscal 2007 and $4&nbsp;million thereafter. In connection
with the adoption of Statement of Financial Accounting Standards
No.&nbsp;142, &#147;Goodwill and Other Intangible Assets,&#148;
as of the beginning of fiscal 2002, goodwill is no longer
amortized but reviewed periodically for impairment.
</FONT>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">During fiscal 2001, Applied established a venture
capital fund, Applied Materials Ventures&nbsp;I, L.P.
(Ventures&nbsp;I), to invest in privately-held, early-stage
companies engaged in developing communications components,
systems and sub-systems. Ventures&nbsp;I&#146;s investment
objectives were subsequently expanded to include systems,
devices and processing technology based on nanotechnology for
specific applications and products. Ventures&nbsp;I is a limited
partnership with Applied as the sole limited partner and an
independent party as the general partner. Applied has committed
to fund $50&nbsp;million in capital contributions, but has
reserved the option to discontinue capital contributions at
$25&nbsp;million. Applied&#146;s capital contributions to
Ventures&nbsp;I totaled approximately $9&nbsp;million at
October&nbsp;27, 2002 and $11&nbsp;million at April&nbsp;27,
2003. As provided for in the partnership agreement, the general
partner has control over investment decisions and operations of
Ventures&nbsp;I. Accordingly, Applied accounts for its
investment using the equity method. Capital contributions, net
of the pro rata share of Ventures&nbsp;I&#146;s results of
operations, have been included in other assets and totaled
$6&nbsp;million at October&nbsp;27, 2002 and $7&nbsp;million at
April&nbsp;27, 2003. Applied does not expect its investment in
Ventures&nbsp;I to have a material effect on its financial
condition or results of operation.
</FONT>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">In January 2003, the Financial Accounting
Standard Board (FASB) issued Interpretation No.&nbsp;46
(FIN&nbsp;46), &#147;Consolidation of Variable Interest
Entities, an interpretation of ARB No.&nbsp;51.&#148;
FIN&nbsp;46 provides guidance on the identification,
classification and accounting of variable interest entities. If
certain criteria are met, Applied may be required to consolidate
Ventures&nbsp;I during the fourth fiscal quarter of 2003.
Applied is in the process of assessing the effect of
FIN&nbsp;46, and does not expect the adoption of FIN&nbsp;46,
which will be effective for interim or annual reporting periods
beginning after June&nbsp;15, 2003, to have a material impact on
its financial condition or results of operations.
</FONT>

<P align="left">
<B><FONT size="2">7)&nbsp;Restructuring, Asset Impairments and
Other Charges</FONT></B>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">During the second fiscal quarter of 2003, Applied
initiated the 2003 Realignment Plan (the Plan) to realign its
infrastructure with current business conditions, resulting in
restructuring, asset impairments, and other charges of
$93&nbsp;million, or $0.04 per share. As a result of the Plan,
Applied will reduce its global workforce by approximately
2,000&nbsp;positions or 14&nbsp;percent. The majority of the
affected employees are based in Santa Clara, California and
Austin, Texas and represent multiple company activities and
functions. The restructuring, asset impairments and other
charges of $93&nbsp;million during the second fiscal quarter of
2003 included $29&nbsp;million of non-cash items, primarily for
fixed asset write-offs. The majority of the cash outlays are
anticipated to occur during fiscal 2003.
</FONT>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">During the first fiscal quarter of 2003, Applied
recorded a pre-tax restructuring charge of $99&nbsp;million, or
$0.04 per share, for employee-related costs and consolidation of
facilities. As a result of this action, Applied reduced its
global workforce by approximately 1,750&nbsp;positions or
11&nbsp;percent. The majority of the affected employees were
based in Santa Clara, California and Austin, Texas and
represented multiple company activities and functions. The
restructuring charge of $99&nbsp;million included no non-cash
items. The majority of the cash outlays have been incurred or
are anticipated to occur in fiscal 2003.
</FONT>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">Restructuring and other items for the first
fiscal quarter of 2002 totaled $85&nbsp;million, or $0.04 per
share. During the first fiscal quarter of 2002, Applied recorded
$8&nbsp;million for in-process research and development expense
in connection with its acquisitions of Schlumberger&#146;s
electron-beam wafer inspection business and Global Knowledge
Services, Inc. (GKS). For further details regarding these
acquisitions, see Note&nbsp;10. Also during the first fiscal
quarter of 2002, Applied recorded a pre-tax restructuring charge
of $77&nbsp;million for employee-related costs, consolidation of
facilities and other costs, and reduced its global workforce by
approximately 1,100&nbsp;positions, or six percent. The majority
of the affected employees were based in Santa Clara, California
and Austin, Texas, and represented multiple company activities
and functions. The restructuring charge of $77&nbsp;million
consisted of $49&nbsp;million of cash outlays and
$28&nbsp;million of non-cash charges, primarily for fixed asset
write-offs.
</FONT>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">At April&nbsp;27, 2003, the restructuring reserve
consisted of $8&nbsp;million related to a restructuring
implemented in the fourth fiscal quarter of 2001,
$10&nbsp;million related to the restructuring implemented in the
first fiscal quarter of 2002, $18&nbsp;million related to the
restructuring implemented in the first fiscal quarter of 2003
and $52&nbsp;million related to the restructuring implemented in
the second fiscal quarter of 2003. Prior years&#146;
</FONT>

<P align="left">
<B><FONT size="2">8) Derivative Financial Instruments</FONT></B>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">In accordance with Statement of Financial
Accounting Standards No.&nbsp;133 (SFAS&nbsp;133),
&#147;Accounting for Derivative Instruments and Hedging
Activities,&#148; all of Applied&#146;s derivative financial
instruments, consisting of forward exchange contracts and
currency option contracts such as Japanese yen, euro and British
pounds are recorded at their fair value on the balance sheet,
either in other current assets or accounts payable and accrued
expenses. Changes in the fair value of derivatives that do not
qualify for hedge treatment, as well as the ineffective portion
of any hedges, must be recognized currently in earnings. The
effective portion of the gain or loss is reported as a component
of accumulated other comprehensive income in stockholders&#146;
equity, and is reclassified into earnings when the hedged
transaction affects earnings. All amounts included in
accumulated other comprehensive income at April&nbsp;27, 2003
will be reclassified to earnings within 12&nbsp;months. Changes
in the fair value of currency option contracts due to changes in
time value are excluded from the assessment of effectiveness,
and are recognized in cost of products sold. The change in
option time value was not material for the three and six months
ended April&nbsp;28, 2002 or April&nbsp;27, 2003. If the
transaction being hedged fails to occur, or if a portion of any
derivative is ineffective, Applied immediately recognizes the
gain or loss on the associated financial instrument in general
and administrative expenses. The amounts recognized due to the
anticipated transactions failing to occur were not material for
the three and six months ended April&nbsp;28, 2002 and
April&nbsp;27, 2003.
</FONT>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">Derivative-related activity in accumulated other
comprehensive income for the six months ended April&nbsp;27,
2003 decreased by $4&nbsp;million, which was comprised of a
$2&nbsp;million net increase in fair value of derivatives,
offset by $6&nbsp;million of net gains reclassified from
accumulated other comprehensive income to earnings.
</FONT>

<TR valign="top">
    <TD></TD>
    <TD>
    <B><I><FONT size="2">Stock Repurchase Program</FONT></I></B></TD>
</TR>

</TABLE>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">Since March 1996, Applied has systematically
repurchased shares of its common stock in the open market to
partially fund its stock-based employee benefit plans. Upon the
expiration of the previous authorization on March&nbsp;22, 2001,
the Board of Directors extended the stock repurchase program and
authorized the repurchase of up to $2&nbsp;billion of
Applied&#146;s common stock in the open market over the
succeeding three years. Under this authorization, Applied will
continue a systematic stock repurchase program and may also make
additional stock repurchases from time to time, depending on
market conditions, stock price and other factors.
</FONT>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">During the six months ended April&nbsp;28, 2002,
Applied repurchased 776,000&nbsp;shares of its common stock at
an average price of $25.22 for a cash outlay of
$20&nbsp;million. During the six months ended April&nbsp;27,
2003, Applied repurchased 7,068,000&nbsp;shares of its common
stock at an average price of $14.14, for a total cash outlay of
$100&nbsp;million.
</FONT>

<P align="left">
<B><FONT size="2">10)&nbsp;Business Combinations</FONT></B>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">On November&nbsp;20, 2001, Applied acquired the
assets of Schlumberger&#146;s electron-beam wafer inspection
business for $66&nbsp;million in cash. In connection with this
acquisition, Applied recorded acquired in-process research and
development expense of $6&nbsp;million and goodwill of
$81&nbsp;million, net of adjustments to the initial purchase
price allocation, partially offset by net liabilities acquired
of $21&nbsp;million. The amount of acquired in-
</FONT>

<P align="center"><FONT size="2">11
</FONT>
<!-- PAGEBREAK -->
<P><HR noshade><P>
<H5 align="left" style="page-break-before:always">&nbsp;</H5><P>

<DIV align="center">
<B><FONT size="2">APPLIED MATERIALS, INC.</FONT></B>
</DIV>

<P align="center">
<B><FONT size="2">NOTES TO CONSOLIDATED CONDENSED FINANCIAL
STATEMENTS&nbsp;&#151;&nbsp;(Continued)</FONT></B>

<DIV align="center">
<FONT size="2">(Unaudited)
</FONT>
</DIV>

<P align="left">
<FONT size="2">process research and development expense was
determined by identifying research projects for which
technological feasibility had not been established and for which
no alternative future use existed. The value of the projects
identified as in-process was determined by calculating the total
development costs incurred, estimating the portion of
development costs related to the aspect of the project that
Applied expected to utilize, and then calculating the current
value of these historical development costs using a Consumer
Price Index adjustment.
</FONT>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">On December&nbsp;3, 2001, Applied acquired GKS, a
provider of advanced data mining services to improve
semiconductor manufacturing yield and efficiency, for
$16&nbsp;million in cash. In connection with this acquisition,
Applied recorded acquired in-process research and development
expense of $2&nbsp;million, goodwill of $6&nbsp;million,
purchased technology of $4&nbsp;million and other items of
$4&nbsp;million. The amount of acquired in-process research and
development expense was determined by identifying research
projects for which technological feasibility had not been
established and for which no alternative future use existed. The
value of the projects identified as in-process was determined by
estimating the future cash flows from the projects once
commercially feasible, discounting the net cash flows back to
their present value at a rate commensurate with the level of
risk and maturity of the projects, and then applying a
percentage-of-completion to the calculated value.
</FONT>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">On April&nbsp;8, 2002, Applied acquired Electron
Vision Corporation, a designer, manufacturer and seller of
e-beam stabilization and curing tools for the semiconductor,
thin film head and micro-fabrication industries, for
$26&nbsp;million in cash. In connection with this acquisition,
Applied recorded goodwill of $13&nbsp;million, net of
adjustments to the initial purchase price allocation, and
purchased technology of $16&nbsp;million, partially offset by
other items of $3 million, primarily for deferred tax
liabilities.
</FONT>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">On April&nbsp;18, 2003, Applied acquired Boxer
Cross, Inc., a producer of a new class of in-line monitoring
systems that provide customers with critical electrical
measurement data for controlling semiconductor processes, for
$14&nbsp;million in cash. In connection with this acquisition,
Applied recorded goodwill of $18&nbsp;million, net of
adjustments to the initial purchase price allocation, and
purchased technology of $3&nbsp;million,<I> </I>partially offset
by other items of $7&nbsp;million, primarily for deferred tax
assets and other liabilities. The in-process research and
development expense was immaterial.
</FONT>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">For all of the purchase business combinations
discussed above, the results of operations prior to the
acquisition dates were not material in relation to those of
Applied for any of the periods presented herein. Goodwill is not
amortized but is reviewed periodically for impairment, and
purchased technology is amortized over its useful life of five
to 10&nbsp;years. These acquisitions have not had, and are not
expected to have, a material effect on Applied&#146;s financial
condition or results of operations.
</FONT>

<P align="left">
<B><FONT size="2">11) Notes Payable</FONT></B>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">Applied has credit facilities for unsecured
borrowings in Japanese yen up to approximately
$160&nbsp;million. The credit facilities are primarily with
Japanese banks at rates indexed to their prime reference rate.
No amounts were outstanding under these credit facilities at
April&nbsp;27, 2003.
</FONT>

<P align="left">
<B><FONT size="2">12) New Accounting Pronouncements</FONT></B>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">In April 2002, the FASB issued Statement of
Financial Accounting Standards (SFAS)&nbsp;No.&nbsp;145
(SFAS&nbsp;145), &#147;Rescission of FASB Statements No.&nbsp;4,
44 and 64, Amendment of FASB Statement No.&nbsp;13, and
Technical Corrections.&#148; SFAS 145 eliminates SFAS&nbsp;4,
&#147;Reporting Gains and Losses from Extinguishment of
Debt,&#148; which required all gains and losses from
extinguishment of debt to be aggregated and, if material,
classified as an extraordinary item. Under SFAS&nbsp;145, such
gains and losses should be classified as extraordinary only if
they meet the criteria of APB Opinion No.&nbsp;30. In addition,
SFAS&nbsp;145 amends SFAS&nbsp;13, &#147;Accounting for
Leases,&#148; to eliminate an inconsistency between the required
accounting for sale-leaseback
</FONT>

<P align="center"><FONT size="2">12
</FONT>

<!-- PAGEBREAK -->
<P><HR noshade><P>
<H5 align="left" style="page-break-before:always">&nbsp;</H5><P>

<DIV align="center">
<B><FONT size="2">APPLIED MATERIALS, INC.</FONT></B>
</DIV>

<P align="center">
<B><FONT size="2">NOTES TO CONSOLIDATED CONDENSED FINANCIAL
STATEMENTS&nbsp;&#151;&nbsp;(Continued)</FONT></B>

<DIV align="center">
<FONT size="2">(Unaudited)
</FONT>
</DIV>

<P align="left">
<FONT size="2">transactions and the required accounting for
certain lease modifications that have economic effects that are
similar to sale-leaseback transactions. Applied does not expect
the adoption of SFAS&nbsp;145, which will become effective at
varying dates from May 2002 to Applied&#146;s fiscal 2003, to
have a material effect on its financial condition or results of
operations.
</FONT>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">In November 2002, The Emerging Issues Task Force
reached a consensus on Issue No.&nbsp;00-21 (EITF&nbsp;00-21),
&#147;Revenue Arrangements with Multiple Deliverables.&#148;
EITF&nbsp;00-21 provides guidance on accounting for arrangements
that involve the delivery of performance of multiple products,
services and/or rights to use assets. Applied is in the process
of assessing the effect of EITF&nbsp;00-21 and does not expect
the adoption of EITF&nbsp;00-21, which will apply to revenue
arrangements beginning in Applied&#146;s fourth fiscal quarter
of 2003, to have a material effect on its financial condition or
results of operations.
</FONT>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">In January 2003, the FASB issued FASB
Interpretation No.&nbsp;46 (FIN&nbsp;46), &#147;Consolidation of
Variable Interest Entities, an interpretation of ARB
No.&nbsp;51.&#148; FIN&nbsp;46 provides guidance on: 1)&nbsp;the
identification of entities for which control is achieved through
means other than through voting rights, known as &#147;variable
interest entities&#148; (VIEs); and 2)&nbsp;which business
enterprise is the primary beneficiary and when it should
consolidate the VIE. This new model for consolidation applies to
entities: 1)&nbsp;where the equity investors (if any) do not
have a controlling financial interest; or 2)&nbsp;whose equity
investment at risk is insufficient to finance that entity&#146;s
activities without receiving additional subordinated financial
support from other parties. In addition, FIN&nbsp;46 requires
that both the primary beneficiary and all other enterprises with
a significant variable interest in a VIE make additional
disclosures. FIN 46 is effective for all new VIEs created or
acquired after January&nbsp;31, 2003. For VIEs created or
acquired prior to February&nbsp;1, 2003, the provisions of
FIN&nbsp;46 must be applied for the first interim or annual
period beginning after June&nbsp;15, 2003. Certain disclosures
are effective immediately. Applied is in the process of
assessing the effect of FIN&nbsp;46, but does not expect its
implementation to have a material effect on its financial
condition or results of operations.
</FONT>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">In April 2003, the FASB issued Statement of
Financial Accounting Standards No.&nbsp;149 (SFAS&nbsp;149),
&#147;Amendment of Statement&nbsp;133 on Derivative Instruments
and Hedging Activities.&#148; This statement amends
SFAS&nbsp;133 to provide clarification on the financial
accounting and reporting of derivative instruments and hedging
activities and requires contracts with similar characteristics
to be accounted for on a comparable basis. Applied is in the
process of assessing the effect of SFAS&nbsp;149 and does not
expect the adoption of it, which will be effective for contracts
entered into or modified after June&nbsp;30, 2003, to have a
material effect on its financial condition or results of
operations.
</FONT>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">In May 2003, the FASB issued Statement of
Financial Accounting Standards No.&nbsp;150 (SFAS&nbsp;150),
&#147;Accounting for Certain Financial Instruments with
Characteristics of both Liabilities and Equity.&#148;
SFAS&nbsp;150 establishes standards on the classification and
measurement of financial instruments with characteristics of
both liabilities and equity. SFAS&nbsp;150 will become effective
for financial instruments entered into or modified after
May&nbsp;31, 2003. Applied is in the process of assessing the
effect of SFAS 150 and does not expect the implementation of the
pronouncement to have a material effect on its financial
condition or results of operations.
</FONT>

<P align="center"><FONT size="2">13
</FONT>

<P align="left">
<B><FONT size="2">Results of Operations</FONT></B>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">Applied is a supplier of semiconductor
manufacturing equipment and services to the global semiconductor
industry. Business activity in the semiconductor and
semiconductor manufacturing equipment industries has been
cyclical; for this and other reasons, Applied&#146;s results of
operations for the three and six months ended April&nbsp;27,
2003 may not necessarily be indicative of future operating
results.
</FONT>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">The continued and prolonged industry downturn,
which Applied believes is the most severe decline in the history
of the semiconductor industry, has resulted in a significant
decrease in demand for manufacturing equipment. Inventory
buildups in telecommunication products, slower than expected
personal computer sales and slow global economic growth have
caused semiconductor companies to re-evaluate their capital
spending and reschedule or cancel existing orders. These factors
resulted in sequential declines in orders that began in the
first fiscal quarter of 2001 and continued through the fourth
fiscal quarter of 2001. Flat orders in the first fiscal quarter
of 2002 were followed by a slight improvement in orders in the
second and third fiscal quarters of 2002 as customers reacted to
an increase in demand for logic integrated circuits. When the
anticipated business did not meet customer expectations, these
customers reduced or deferred capital equipment spending. At the
same time, these customers were faced with weak market
conditions, geopolitical uncertainties, financing difficulties
and other challenges. These factors resulted in further
sequential declines in orders from the third fiscal quarter of
2002 through the second fiscal quarter of 2003.
</FONT>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">Applied received new orders of $971&nbsp;million
for the second fiscal quarter of 2003 compared to
$1.0&nbsp;billion for the first fiscal quarter of 2003 and
$1.7&nbsp;billion for the second fiscal quarter of 2002,
reflecting the continued and prolonged downturn in the
semiconductor industry.
</FONT>

<P align="center"><FONT size="2">14
</FONT>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">Applied&#146;s backlog for the most recent three
fiscal quarters was as follows: $2.8&nbsp;billion at
April&nbsp;27, 2003, compared to $3.1&nbsp;billion at
January&nbsp;26, 2003 and $3.2&nbsp;billion at October&nbsp;27,
2002. Backlog consists only of orders for which written
authorizations have been accepted, shipment dates within
12&nbsp;months have been assigned and revenue has not been
recognized. Due to possible customer changes in delivery
schedules and cancellations of orders, Applied&#146;s backlog at
any particular date is not necessarily indicative of actual
sales for any future periods.
</FONT>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">During fiscal 2002, net sales remained relatively
flat for the first and second fiscal quarters, followed by a
modest increase in the third fiscal quarter. In the fourth
fiscal quarter of 2002, net sales declined slightly from the
third fiscal quarter of 2002 and declined further during the
first fiscal quarter of 2003. Net sales for the second fiscal
quarter of 2003 increased five percent from the preceding
quarter of 2003 but decreased four percent from the second
fiscal quarter of 2002. Net sales for the six months ended
April&nbsp;27, 2003 remained flat with the six months ended
April&nbsp;28, 2002. The overall sales level remained relatively
low, reflecting the continued uncertainties associated with the
prolonged downturn and the macro-economic climate discussed
previously. Net sales by region for the second fiscal quarters
of 2002 and 2003 were as follows (dollars in millions):
</FONT>

    <FONT size="2">Includes China.
    </FONT></TD>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">As indicated in the above table, revenue from all
the other regions remained relatively consistent with the prior
year&#146;s level, except for Korea, Japan and Taiwan. Revenue
from Korea increased significantly from the prior year due to
customers&#146; fab upgrades and purchases of new 300mm tools.
Revenue in Japan increased from the prior year due to an
increase in customers&#146; investments for new technology
implementation. The
</FONT>

<P align="center"><FONT size="2">15
</FONT>

<!-- PAGEBREAK -->
<P><HR noshade><P>
<H5 align="left" style="page-break-before:always">&nbsp;</H5><P>

<DIV align="left">
<FONT size="2">revenue decrease in Taiwan reflected lowered
factory utilization, which drove the reduced capital investment
plans.
</FONT>
</DIV>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">In response to the industry downturn, Applied
announced a 2003 Realignment Plan (the Plan) on March&nbsp;17,
2003 in order to align its infrastructure with business
conditions. Applied expects to incur pretax charges of up to
$425&nbsp;million over four quarters starting from the second
fiscal quarter of 2003. The Plan has two elements: first,
restructuring actions (including consolidation of facilities and
a reduction in workforce); and second, refocused product
development and cost reduction programs. Both parts of the Plan
will result in charges to income across multiple categories, as
incurred, such as cost of products sold and operating expenses.
During the second fiscal quarter of 2003, Applied began
implementing the Plan and incurred pretax charges totaling
approximately $152&nbsp;million. Activities to date consisted
principally of employee-related actions, facilities
consolidation, refocused product development and cost reduction
programs. These charges were incurred across the following
categories: restructuring, asset impairments and other charges
of $93&nbsp;million; costs of products sold of $49&nbsp;million;
and research, development and engineering expense of
$10&nbsp;million.
</FONT>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">Gross margin was 33.7&nbsp;percent for the second
fiscal quarter of 2003, compared to 37.0&nbsp;percent for the
first fiscal quarter of 2003 and 40.0&nbsp;percent for the
second fiscal quarter of 2002. Gross margin was
35.3&nbsp;percent for the six months ended April&nbsp;27, 2003
compared to 39.3&nbsp;percent for the six months ended
April&nbsp;28, 2002. The decrease in gross margin during the
first six months of fiscal 2003 was mainly due to charges
incurred from the refocused product development and cost
reduction programs associated with the Plan.
</FONT>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">Operating expenses included expenses related to
research, development and engineering (RD&#38;E), marketing and
selling (M&#38;S), general and administrative (G&#38;A), and
restructuring, asset impairments and other. Expenses related to
RD&#38;E, M&#38;S and G&#38;A were $394&nbsp;million for the
second fiscal quarter of 2003, compared to $408&nbsp;million for
the first fiscal quarter of 2003 and $423&nbsp;million for the
second fiscal quarter of 2002. These expenses were
$802&nbsp;million for the six months ended April&nbsp;27, 2003,
versus $824&nbsp;million for the comparable period of fiscal
2002. The reduction in these expenses was attributable to
ongoing cost control measures and reduction of discretionary
spending.
</FONT>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">Operating expenses also included restructuring,
asset impairments and other charges, which for the second fiscal
quarter of 2003 totaled $93 million. There were no such charges
during the second fiscal quarter of fiscal 2002. Restructuring,
asset impairments and other charges were $192&nbsp;million and
$85&nbsp;million for the six months ended April&nbsp;27, 2003
and April&nbsp;28, 2002, respectively. These charges consisted
of employee related costs and consolidation of facilities to
better realign Applied&#146;s infrastructure with business
conditions. For further details, see Note&nbsp;7 of Notes to
Consolidated Condensed Financial Statements.
</FONT>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">Net interest income was $34&nbsp;million and
$26&nbsp;million for the three months ended April&nbsp;28, 2002
and April&nbsp;27, 2003, respectively, and was $71&nbsp;million
and $50&nbsp;million for the six months ended April&nbsp;28,
2002 and April&nbsp;27, 2003, respectively. Lower net interest
income in 2003 was principally attributable to lower average
interest rates.
</FONT>

<P align="left">
<B><FONT size="2">Financial Condition, Liquidity and Capital
Resources</FONT></B>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">During the second fiscal quarter of 2003, Applied
increased its cash, cash equivalents and short-term investments
by $290&nbsp;million from October&nbsp;27, 2002 to
$5.22&nbsp;billion at April&nbsp;27, 2003. Applied generally has
generated cash from operating activities, primarily from net
income/loss, as adjusted to exclude the effect of non-cash
charges, and working capital management. Applied has not
undertaken any significant external financing activities for
several years.
</FONT>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">Applied generated cash from operating activities
of $401&nbsp;million for the six months ended April&nbsp;27,
2003. The primary sources of cash were from an effect of
non-cash charges, such as depreciation and amortization
expenses, reductions in accounts receivable and inventories,
which were offset by a decrease in payables and the net loss for
the six months ended April&nbsp;27, 2003. Applied utilized
programs to sell accounts receivable of $294&nbsp;million for
the six months ended April&nbsp;27, 2003. These receivable sales
had the effect of increasing cash and reducing accounts
receivable and days sales outstanding. Applied has not
experienced any losses under
</FONT>

<P align="center"><FONT size="2">16
</FONT>

<!-- PAGEBREAK -->
<P><HR noshade><P>
<H5 align="left" style="page-break-before:always">&nbsp;</H5><P>

<DIV align="left">
<FONT size="2">these programs. Days sales outstanding was
61&nbsp;days at the end of the second fiscal quarter of 2003,
compared to 77&nbsp;days at the end of the first fiscal quarter
of 2003. For further details regarding accounts receivable
sales, see Note&nbsp;3 of Notes to Consolidated Condensed
Financial Statements. Inventories were reduced by
$159&nbsp;million during the six months ended April&nbsp;27,
2003, due primarily to product refocus efforts and ongoing
inventory management and reduction programs.
</FONT>
</DIV>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">Applied used $232&nbsp;million of cash for
investing activities during the six months ended April&nbsp;27,
2003. Capital expenditures, net of retirements, were
$101&nbsp;million. The majority of capital expenditures
consisted of the purchase of facilities in Hillsboro, Oregon for
$52 million that was previously held under a synthetic lease.
The remainder of the capital spending consisted of expenditures
for application laboratories, equipment and related facilities.
Investing activities also included purchases and sales of
short-term investments, which used $131&nbsp;million of cash.
</FONT>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">Applied used $27&nbsp;million of cash for
financing activities for the six months ended April&nbsp;27,
2003, consisting of repayments of debt and repurchases of stock,
offset by issuances of common stock under employee stock plans.
</FONT>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">To date, Applied has not declared or paid cash
dividends to its stockholders due to a number of factors,
including the volatile nature of the semiconductor industry and
Applied&#146;s intention to reinvest in its business.
</FONT>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">Although cash requirements will fluctuate based
on the timing and extent of many factors, Applied&#146;s
management believes that cash generated from operations,
together with the liquidity provided by existing cash balances
and borrowing capability, will be sufficient to satisfy
Applied&#146;s liquidity requirements for the next
12&nbsp;months. For further details regarding Applied&#146;s
operating, investing and financing activities see the
Consolidated Condensed Statements of Cash Flows.
</FONT>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">The preparation of financial statements and

<P align="left">
<B><FONT size="2">Trends, Risks and Uncertainties</FONT></B>

<DIV>&nbsp;</DIV>

<TABLE width="100%" border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0">

<TR>
    <TD width="3%"></TD>
    <TD width="97%"></TD>
</TR>

<TR valign="top">
    <TD></TD>
    <TD>
    <B><I><FONT size="2">The industry that Applied serves is highly
    volatile and unpredictable.</FONT></I></B></TD>
</TR>

</TABLE>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">As a supplier to the semiconductor industry,
Applied is subject to the business cycles that characterize the
industry&nbsp;&#151; the timing, length and volatility of these
cycles are difficult to predict. The semiconductor industry has
historically been cyclical because of sudden changes in demand
for semiconductors and manufacturing capacity, including
capacity utilizing the latest technology. The rate of changes in
demand, including end demand, is accelerating, and the effect of
these changes on Applied is occurring sooner, exacerbating the
volatility of these cycles. These changes have affected the
timing and amounts of customers&#146; capital equipment
purchases and investments in new technology, and continue to
affect Applied&#146;s net sales, gross margin and results of
operations. In addition to affecting Applied&#146;s customers
and suppliers, these business cycles also challenge key
management, engineering and other employees of Applied.
</FONT>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">During periods of declining demand for
semiconductor manufacturing equipment, customers typically
reduce purchases, delay delivery of products and/or cancel
orders. During downturns, Applied must be able to timely align
its cost structure with prevailing market conditions, to
successfully manage its assets, and to effectively motivate and
retain key employees. Historically, Applied has reduced its
workforce, consolidated facilities and reallocated resources
during downturns.
</FONT>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">The semiconductor equipment industry is currently
experiencing a continued and prolonged downturn, which
management believes is the most severe decline in history. In
response to this downturn, Applied initiated the Plan announced
on March&nbsp;17, 2003 in order to better align its
infrastructure with business conditions. If Applied is unable to
implement the Plan according to the timetable and to the extent
</FONT>

<P align="center"><FONT size="2">17
</FONT>

<!-- PAGEBREAK -->
<P><HR noshade><P>
<H5 align="left" style="page-break-before:always">&nbsp;</H5><P>

<DIV align="left">
<FONT size="2">anticipated, if implementation negatively affects
Applied&#146;s net sales or profitability, or if Applied does
not maintain cost controls that effectively align its costs with
market conditions, Applied&#146;s business, financial condition
or results of operations may be negatively affected. Management
cannot predict the timing of a recovery and the industry&#146;s
rate of growth in such a recovery, both of which will be
affected by many factors, including the global uncertainties
discussed herein.
</FONT>
</DIV>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">During periods of rapid growth, Applied must be
able to acquire and/or develop sufficient manufacturing capacity
and inventory to meet customer demand, and to attract, hire,
assimilate and retain a sufficient number of qualified people.
If Applied is unable to achieve its objectives in a timely
manner during changes in business conditions, there could be a
material adverse effect on its business, financial condition and
results of operations.
</FONT>

<DIV>&nbsp;</DIV>

<TABLE width="100%" border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0">

<TR>
    <TD width="3%"></TD>
    <TD width="97%"></TD>
</TR>

<TR valign="top">
    <TD></TD>
    <TD>
    <B><I><FONT size="2">Applied is exposed to the risks of
    operating a global business.</FONT></I></B></TD>
</TR>

</TABLE>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">For the first half of fiscal 2003, approximately
70&nbsp;percent of Applied&#146;s revenues resulted from sales
outside the United States, with an increasing percentage of
sales to customers in Asia. Certain manufacturing facilities and
suppliers of Applied are also located outside the United States.
Managing Applied&#146;s global operations presents challenges,
including periodic regional economic downturns, trade balance
issues, varying business conditions and demands, political
instability, variations in enforcement of intellectual property
and contract rights in different jurisdictions, differences in
the ability to develop relationships with suppliers and other
local businesses, changes in U.S. and international laws and
regulations including U.S. export restrictions, fluctuations in
interest and currency exchange rates, the ability to provide
sufficient levels of technical support in different locations,
cultural differences, shipping delays and terrorist acts or acts
of war, among other risks. Many of these challenges are present
in China, which represents a large potential market for
semiconductor equipment and is where Applied anticipates
significant opportunity for growth. Global uncertainties with
respect to: 1)&nbsp;economic growth rates in various countries,
including countries affected by Severe Acute Respiratory
Syndrome (SARS); 2)&nbsp;sustainability of demand for
electronics products; 3)&nbsp;capital spending by semiconductor
manufacturers; 4)&nbsp;price weakness for certain semiconductor
devices; and 5)&nbsp;political instability, terrorism, acts of
war, or epidemics in regions where Applied has operations or
sales, including Asia and Israel, may also affect Applied&#146;s
business, financial condition and results of operations.
</FONT>

<DIV>&nbsp;</DIV>

<TABLE width="100%" border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0">

<TR>
    <TD width="3%"></TD>
    <TD width="97%"></TD>
</TR>

<TR valign="top">
    <TD></TD>
    <TD>
    <B><I><FONT size="2">Applied operates in a highly competitive
    industry characterized by increasingly rapid technological
    changes.</FONT></I></B></TD>
</TR>

</TABLE>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">While operating in a highly competitive
environment, Applied&#146;s future success is heavily dependent
upon effective development, commercialization and customer
acceptance of its new products over those of its competitors.
Specifically, these risks may include, but are not limited to,
Applied&#146;s ability to timely and cost effectively:
1)&nbsp;develop new products, services and technologies,
including those utilizing new materials, such as copper and
low-k materials; 2)&nbsp;develop improvements to existing
products, services and technologies; 3)&nbsp;develop new markets
in the semiconductor industry for Applied&#146;s products and
services; 4)&nbsp;introduce new products and services to the
marketplace; 5)&nbsp;achieve market acceptance and accurately
forecast product demand; 6)&nbsp;qualify new or improved
products for volume manufacturing with its customers;
7)&nbsp;commence and adjust production to meet customer demands;
and 8)&nbsp;price products and services appropriately. The
development, introduction and support of an increasingly broad
set of new or improved products and technologies, including
those enabling the transition to smaller device feature sizes,
new materials and 300mm wafers, grow increasingly complex and
expensive over time. Such new or improved products may involve
higher costs and reduced efficiencies compared to Applied&#146;s
more established products and could adversely affect
Applied&#146;s gross margins. If Applied does not develop and
introduce new or improved products, services and technologies in
a timely and cost-effective manner in response to changing
market conditions or customer requirements, its competitive
position, financial condition and results of operations could be
materially and adversely affected.
</FONT>

</FONT>

    <B><I><FONT size="2">Applied is exposed to risks as a result of
    ongoing changes in the semiconductor industry.</FONT></I></B></TD>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">The semiconductor industry is characterized by
ongoing changes. More complex technology requirements, the
changing information technology cost structure, the increasing
significance of consumer electronics as a driver for chip demand
and the related focus on lower prices, and the growing type and
variety of chips and applications, have created challenges for
Applied. These factors, along with the increasing segmentation
of applications in the semiconductor industry and resulting
greater differentiation of interests among semiconductor
manufacturers, as well as an increasing percentage of business
from customers in Asia, are increasing the need for customer
partnering, collective research and development efforts and
process integration support, and are driving the importance of
spares and services as an expanding portion of semiconductor
equipment suppliers&#146; business. If Applied does not
successfully manage the risks resulting from these changes, its
business, financial condition and results of operation could be
materially and adversely affected.
</FONT>

<DIV>&nbsp;</DIV>

<TABLE width="100%" border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0">

    <TD>
    <B><I><FONT size="2">Applied is exposed to risks associated with
    a highly concentrated customer base.</FONT></I></B></TD>
</TR>

</TABLE>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">Applied&#146;s customer base is highly
concentrated. Orders from a relatively limited number of
semiconductor manufacturers have accounted for, and likely will
continue to account for, a substantial portion of Applied&#146;s
net sales, which may lead customers to demand pricing and other
terms less favorable to Applied. In addition, sales to any
single customer may vary significantly from quarter to quarter.
If current customers delay, cancel or do not place orders,
Applied may not be able to replace these orders with new orders.
As Applied&#146;s products are configured to customer
specifications, changing, rescheduling or canceling orders may
result in significant and often non-recoverable costs. The
resulting fluctuations in the amount of and terms of orders
could have a material adverse effect on Applied&#146;s business,
financial condition and results of operations.
</FONT>

<DIV>&nbsp;</DIV>

<TABLE width="100%" border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0">

<TR>
    <TD width="3%"></TD>
    <TD width="97%"></TD>
</TR>

<TR valign="top">
    <TD></TD>
    <TD>
    <B><I><FONT size="2">Manufacturing interruptions or delays could
    affect Applied&#146;s ability to meet customer
    demand.</FONT></I></B></TD>
</TR>

</TABLE>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">Applied&#146;s business depends on its ability to
manufacture products that meet the rapidly changing demands of
its customers. Applied&#146;s ability to manufacture depends in
part on the timely delivery of parts, components, and
subassemblies (collectively parts) from suppliers. Some key
parts may be obtained only from a single supplier or a limited
group of suppliers. In addition, Applied outsources certain
manufacturing activities. Significant interruptions of
manufacturing operations as a result of the failure or inability
of suppliers to timely deliver quality parts, outsourcing
difficulties, natural disasters (such as earthquakes or
tornadoes), or other causes (such as information technology or
infrastructure failures, regional economic downturns, political
instability, terrorism, acts of war, or epidemics) could result
in delayed product deliveries or manufacturing inefficiencies.
Any or all of these factors could materially and adversely
affect Applied&#146;s business, financial condition and results
of operations.
</FONT>

<DIV>&nbsp;</DIV>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">Applied&#146;s success depends in large part on
its ability to attract, retain and motivate key employees,
including those in managerial, technical, marketing and support
roles. Achieving this objective may be difficult due to global
economic uncertainty, the current industry downturn, workforce
reductions and changes in management. If Applied does not
successfully attract, retain or motivate key employees, the
Company&#146;s operating results and ability to capitalize on
its opportunities may be adversely affected.

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">Applied is subject to various risks related to:
1)&nbsp;new, different, inconsistent or even conflicting laws,
rules and regulations that may be enacted by legislative bodies
and/or regulatory agencies in the regions in which Applied
operates and with which Applied must comply; and
2)&nbsp;disagreements or disputes between national or regional
regulatory agencies related to international trade.

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">For example, the World Trade
Organization&nbsp;(WTO) has determined that the U.S. Foreign
Sales Corporation&nbsp;(FSC) and Extraterritorial
Income&nbsp;(ETI) exclusion constitute prohibited export
subsidies warranting the possible imposition of trade sanctions
on certain goods, including semiconductor manufacturing
equipment. Applied has benefited from FSC and ETI tax
provisions. The elimination of these tax benefits or
</FONT>

</FONT>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">During fiscal 2002, Applied filed an application
with the SEC for an exemptive order confirming that it is not
subject to the Investment Company Act of 1940 (the Act), which
requires companies primarily engaged in the business of
investing in securities to comply with additional rules and
regulations. Largely due to the industry downturn,
Applied&#146;s ratios of investments to total assets and of
interest income to net income have increased, resulting in the
risk that Applied could be deemed to be covered by the Act. If
the SEC does not grant the exemption, Applied may have to take
other actions that could adversely affect its results of
operations in order not to be subject to the Act.

operational matters; 2)&nbsp;the inability to realize expected
synergies resulting from the acquisition; 3)&nbsp;failure to
commercialize purchased technology; and 4)&nbsp;impairment of
acquired intangible assets as a result of technological
advancements or worse-than-expected performance of the acquired
company. Mergers and acquisitions are inherently subject to
multiple significant risks, and the inability to effectively
manage these risks could materially and adversely affect
Applied&#146;s business, financial condition and results of
operations.

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">Applied currently is, and in the future may be,
involved in legal proceedings or claims regarding patent
infringement, intellectual property rights, antitrust,
environmental regulations, securities, contracts, employment and
other matters (see Part&nbsp;II below). In addition, from time
to time, Applied receives notification from customers who
believe that Applied owes them indemnification or other
obligations related to infringement claims made against the
customers by third parties. These legal proceedings and claims,
whether with or without merit, are time-consuming and expensive
to prosecute or defend and divert management&#146;s attention
and resources. There can be no assurance regarding the outcome
of current or future legal proceedings or claims. In addition,
Applied&#146;s intellectual property rights may not provide
significant competitive advantages if they are circumvented,
invalidated or obsoleted by the rapid pace of technological
change. Furthermore, the laws of other countries permit the
protection of Applied&#146;s proprietary rights to varying
extents, compared to U.S. laws. Applied&#146;s success is
dependent in part upon the protection of its intellectual
property rights. Infringement of Applied&#146;s rights by a
third party could result in uncompensated lost market and
revenue opportunities for Applied. If Applied is not able to
resolve a claim, negotiate a settlement of the matter, obtain
necessary licenses on commercially reasonable terms, and/or
successfully prosecute or defend its position, Applied&#146;s
business, financial condition and results of operations could be
materially and adversely affected.
</FONT>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;

disclosure controls and procedures as defined in

it files or submits under the Exchange Act is recorded,
processed, summarized and reported within the time periods
specified in Securities and Exchange Commission rules and forms.

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;

Applied&#146;s internal controls or other factors that could
significantly affect these controls subsequent to the date of
their evaluation and up to the filing date of this Quarterly
Report on Form&nbsp;10-Q. Since there were no significant
deficiencies or material weaknesses identified, no corrective
actions were required.

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">It should be noted that any system of controls,
however well designed and operated, can provide only reasonable,
and not absolute, assurance that the objectives of the system
are met. In addition, the design of any control system is based
in part upon certain assumptions about the likelihood of future
events. Because of these and other inherent limitations of
control systems, there can be no assurance that any design will
succeed in achieving its stated goals under all potential future
conditions, regardless of how remote.

<P align="center">
<B><FONT size="2">PART II.</FONT></B>

<DIV align="center">
<B><FONT size="2">OTHER INFORMATION</FONT></B>
</DIV>

<!-- link2 "Item 1. Legal Proceedings" -->

<P align="left">
<B><FONT size="2">Item&nbsp;1.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<I>Legal
Proceedings</I></FONT></B>

<P align="left">
<B><FONT size="2">Novellus</FONT></B>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">On June&nbsp;13, 1997, after Varian Associates,
Inc. (Varian) failed to respond to requests by Applied to
discuss certain patent issues, Applied filed a lawsuit against
Varian captioned Applied Materials, Inc. v. Varian Associates,
Inc. (case no.&nbsp;C-97-20523-RMW) in the United States
District Court for the Northern District of California, alleging
infringement of several of Applied&#146;s patents concerning PVD
technology. On July&nbsp;7, 1997, Applied amended that action to
allege infringement of those same Applied PVD patents against
Novellus Systems, Inc. (Novellus) and to add Novellus as a
defendant, as a result of Novellus&#146; acquisition of
Varian&#146;s thin film systems PVD business. On June&nbsp;23,
1997, Novellus filed a separate lawsuit against Applied
captioned Novellus Systems, Inc. v. Applied Materials, Inc.
(case no.&nbsp;C-97-20551-EAI) in the United States District
Court for the Northern District of California, alleging
infringement by Applied of several PVD technology patents that
were formerly owned by Varian. Novellus seeks damages for past
infringement, a permanent injunction, treble damages for willful
infringement, pre-judgment interest and attorneys&#146; fees. In
September 2000, Applied and Varian settled their disputes, and
on October&nbsp;3, 2000, Applied&#146;s claims against Varian
and Varian&#146;s claims and counterclaims against Applied were
dismissed with prejudice with respect to the Inova system as it
was made and sold as of May&nbsp;7, 1997. The litigation with
Novellus continues. Discovery has closed in the actions. The
trial date of May&nbsp;27, 2003 has been rescheduled to
January&nbsp;20, 2004. Applied believes it has meritorious
claims and defenses and intends to pursue them vigorously.
</FONT>

<P align="left">
<B><FONT size="2">Axcelis Technologies</FONT></B>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">On January&nbsp;8, 2001, Axcelis Technologies,
Inc. (Axcelis), formerly a subsidiary of Eaton Corporation,
filed a lawsuit in the United States District Court for the
District of Massachusetts, captioned Axcelis Technologies, Inc.
v. Applied Materials, Inc. (case no.&nbsp;01-10029 DPW). The
lawsuit alleges that Applied infringes a patent concerning ion
implantation owned by Axcelis. The complaint also alleges
various Massachusetts state and common law tortious interference
and unfair competition claims. Axcelis seeks a preliminary and
permanent injunction, damages, costs and attorneys&#146; fees.
On April&nbsp;12, 2001, Applied answered the complaint by
denying all allegations and counterclaimed for declaratory
judgment of invalidity and non-infringement, and violations of
various unfair and deceptive trade practices laws. Applied seeks
damages, a permanent injunction, costs and attorneys&#146; fees.
Fact and expert discovery have closed. On December&nbsp;10,
2002, the Court issued a ruling interpreting the claims of the
patent. Summary judgment motions have been filed and argued and
are pending before the Court. The previously set trial date of
May&nbsp;27, 2003 has been rescheduled. Trial on infringement
issues only is now scheduled to begin on June&nbsp;16, 2003.
Applied believes it has meritorious defenses and counterclaims
to the action and intends to pursue them vigorously.
</FONT>

<P align="left">
<B><FONT size="2">Linear Technology</FONT></B>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">On March&nbsp;2, 2001, Linear Technology Corp.
(LTC)&nbsp;filed a third party complaint against Applied in the
United States District Court for the Eastern District of Texas,
captioned Texas Instruments, Inc. v. Linear Technology Corp. v.
Applied Materials, Inc. (case no.&nbsp;2-01-CV4 (DF)). The
complaint against Applied alleged that Applied is obligated to
indemnify LTC and defend LTC for certain claims in the
underlying patent infringement lawsuit brought by Texas
Instruments, Inc. (TI) against LTC. The complaint also alleged
claims for breach of contract, breach of warranty, and various
unfair business practices. In the complaint, LTC alleged that,
before LTC purchased certain equipment from Applied, Applied
failed to disclose to LTC that TI previously had won a jury
verdict against Hyundai Electronics Industries Co., Ltd.
(Hyundai) for patent infringement based on Hyundai&#146;s use of
certain semiconductor equipment including some Applied tools.
LTC&#146;s Texas lawsuit against Applied sought indemnification
and damages from Applied and an order requiring Applied to
defend LTC in the underlying lawsuit with TI. On
January&nbsp;15, 2002, the Court granted TI&#146;s motion to
sever Applied and the other third party defendants from the
action and dismissed LTC&#146;s action
</FONT>

<P align="center"><FONT size="2">22
</FONT>

<!-- PAGEBREAK -->
<P><HR noshade><P>
<H5 align="left" style="page-break-before:always">&nbsp;</H5><P>

<DIV align="left">
<FONT size="2">against Applied and the other third party
defendants without prejudice. On March&nbsp;12, 2002, LTC filed
a complaint against Applied in the Superior Court for the County
of Santa Clara, captioned Linear Technology Corp. v. Applied
Materials, Inc., Novellus Systems, Inc. and Tokyo Electron Ltd.,
(case no.&nbsp;CV806004) alleging claims for breach of contract,
fraud and deceit, negligent misrepresentation, suppression of
fact, unfair competition, breach of warranty, express
contractual indemnity, implied equitable indemnity and
declaratory relief. On November&nbsp;12, 2002, LTC filed an
amended complaint in the Santa Clara action asserting
essentially the same claims as in the original complaint but
adding an additional assertion that LTC and TI have settled
their litigation. In the amended complaint, LTC seeks damages,
punitive damages, injunctive relief and restitution. LTC also
seeks costs and attorneys&#146; fees including costs and
attorneys&#146; fees for the TI litigation. LTC has also
asserted similar claims against certain other semiconductor
equipment manufacturers. Applied&#146;s motion to dismiss the
amended complaint was granted in part. No trial date has been
set. Applied believes that it has meritorious defenses and
intends to pursue them vigorously.
</FONT>
</DIV>

<P align="left">
<B><FONT size="2">Semitool</FONT></B>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">On June&nbsp;11, 2001, Semitool, Inc. (Semitool)
filed a lawsuit against Applied in the United States District
Court for the Northern District of California, captioned
Semitool, Inc. v. Applied Materials, Inc. (case
no.&nbsp;CV-01-2277 CRB). The lawsuit alleged that Applied
infringed a patent concerning seed repair and electroplating
owned by Semitool. Semitool sought a preliminary and permanent
injunction, damages, costs and attorneys&#146; fees. On
July&nbsp;12, 2001, before Applied had answered the complaint,
Semitool voluntarily dismissed its action against Applied in the
Northern District of California. On the same day, Semitool filed
a substantially identical action against Applied in the United
States District Court for the District of Oregon captioned
Semitool, Inc. v. Applied Materials, Inc. (case
no.&nbsp;CV&#146;01-1066&nbsp;AS). On July&nbsp;13, 2001,
Applied filed a declaratory judgment action against Semitool in
the Northern District of California captioned Applied Materials,
Inc. v. Semitool, Inc. (case no.&nbsp;CV-01-2673&nbsp;BZ). In
that action, Applied seeks a declaration that Applied has not
infringed the Semitool patent and that Semitool&#146;s patent is
invalid and unenforceable. Applied also seeks costs and
attorneys&#146; fees. The California Court has ordered
Applied&#146;s action against Semitool transferred to the
District of Oregon. The actions are proceeding together in
Oregon. Semitool has also asserted similar claims against
certain other semiconductor equipment manufacturers. The Oregon
Court has issued an order interpreting the patent claims and has
rescheduled the trial date from June&nbsp;30, 2003 to
February&nbsp;3, 2004. Applied believes it has meritorious
claims and defenses and intends to pursue them vigorously.
</FONT>

<P align="left">
<B><FONT size="2">David Scharf</FONT></B>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">On July&nbsp;31, 2001, David Scharf, an
individual, filed a lawsuit against Applied in the United States
District Court for the Central District of California, captioned
David Scharf v. Applied Materials, Inc. (case no.&nbsp;01-06580
AHM). The lawsuit alleges that Applied has infringed, has
induced others to infringe and has contributed to others&#146;
infringement of a patent concerning color synthesizing scanning
electron microscope technology. Mr.&nbsp;Scharf seeks a
preliminary and permanent injunction, damages and costs. Applied
has answered the complaint and counterclaimed for declaratory
judgment of non-infringement and invalidity. On May&nbsp;10,
2002, Mr.&nbsp;Scharf filed a request for re-examination of his
own patent. On June&nbsp;26, 2002, the case was removed from the
Court&#146;s active docket after the parties stipulated to stay
the case pending the results of that re-examination. On
July&nbsp;11, 2002, Applied filed its own request for
re-examination of Scharf&#146;s patent with the Patent and
Trademark Office. Applied&#146;s request for re-examination was
granted on September&nbsp;19, 2002. Applied believes it has
meritorious defenses and counterclaims and intends to pursue
them vigorously.
</FONT>

<P align="left">
<B><FONT size="2">ASMI</FONT></B>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">On August&nbsp;27, 2002, ASM America, Inc. and
ASM International, N.V. (collectively ASMI) filed a lawsuit
against Applied in the United States District Court for the
District of Arizona, captioned ASM America, Inc. and ASM
International, N.V. v. Applied Materials, Inc. (case
no.&nbsp;Civ&#146;02 1660 PHX SMM). The lawsuit seeks a judicial
declaration that ASMI does not infringe six patents belonging to
Applied that relate to remote cleaning of CVD chambers and to
deposition of silicon nitride. The suit also seeks a judicial
</FONT>

<P align="center"><FONT size="2">23
</FONT>

<!-- PAGEBREAK -->
<P><HR noshade><P>
<H5 align="left" style="page-break-before:always">&nbsp;</H5><P>

<DIV align="left">
<FONT size="2">declaration that two of those six patents are
invalid. On December&nbsp;16, 2002, Applied responded to the
complaint by denying the allegations and counterclaiming for
infringement of two of the patents related to remote cleaning of
CVD chambers. Applied seeks damages, a preliminary and permanent
injunction, costs and attorneys&#146; fees. Applied also moved
to dismiss the complaint with respect to four of the patents and
moved for a more definitive statement with respect to two of
ASMI&#146;s causes of action. ASMI moved for summary judgment
that it has not infringed the same four patents that are the
subject of Applied&#146;s motion to dismiss. No trial date has
been set. Applied believes it has meritorious defenses and
counterclaims and intends to pursue them vigorously.
</FONT>
</DIV>

<P align="left">
<B><FONT size="2">Varian Semiconductor Equipment Associates,
Inc.</FONT></B>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">On September&nbsp;13, 2002, Varian Semiconductor
Equipment Associates, Inc. filed a demand for arbitration with
the American Arbitration Association asserting that Applied
Materials has breached a patent license agreement between Varian
and Applied Materials dated January&nbsp;1, 1992. Varian seeks
to recover royalties, interest and attorneys&#146; fees. The
arbitration hearing on whether the products are covered by the
license agreement has concluded. On May&nbsp;2, 2003, the
arbitration panel issued an interim decision finding that some,
but not all, of the products at issue were subject to the
agreement. The arbitration panel next will consider whether the
asserted claims of the patents under which those products were
found to be covered are valid. Applied Materials believes that
it has meritorious defenses and intends to pursue them
vigorously.
</FONT>

<P align="left">
<B><FONT size="2">Robert Bosch GmbH</FONT></B>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">On October&nbsp;10, 2002, Robert Bosch GmbH
(Bosch), a German company, filed a lawsuit against Applied in
the United States District Court for the District of Delaware,
captioned Robert Bosch GmbH v. Applied Materials, Inc. (civil
action no. 02-1523). The lawsuit alleges that Applied infringes
two patents owned by Bosch related to anisotrophic etching.
Bosch seeks a preliminary and permanent injunction, damages,
costs and attorneys&#146; fees. Applied has answered the
complaint and counterclaimed for declaratory judgment of
non-infringement and invalidity. No trial date has been set.
Applied believes it has meritorious defenses and intends to
pursue them vigorously.
</FONT>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">From time to time, Applied receives notification
from customers claiming that such customers are entitled to
indemnification or other obligations from Applied related to
infringement claims made against the customers by third parties.
In addition, Applied is subject to various other legal
proceedings and claims, either asserted or unasserted, that
arise in the ordinary course of business. Although the outcome
of these claims cannot be predicted with certainty, Applied does
not believe that any of these other existing legal matters will
have a material adverse effect on its financial condition or
results of operations.
</FONT>

<P align="left">
<B><FONT size="2">2.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Other
Matters</FONT></B>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">On April&nbsp;30, 2003, Applied announced the
appointment of Michael&nbsp;R. Splinter as president, chief
executive officer (CEO)&nbsp;and a member of its Board of
Directors. As CEO, Mr.&nbsp;Splinter succeeded James&nbsp;C.
Morgan, who will continue as chairman of the Board of Directors,
and as president, he succeeded Dan Maydan, who will be president
emeritus and remain a member of the Board of Directors. Before
joining Applied, Mr. Splinter worked for nearly 20&nbsp;years at
Intel Corporation, where most recently, he was executive vice
president and director of the Sales and Marketing Group.
</FONT>
